        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239194067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10126268029077977690">Original review 2012:<br/><br/><i>" He took his pain and turned it into something beautiful " </i><br/><br/>Harrington's writing is the kind that makes you stop while you're reading - just to re-read a sentence, to say it out loud, so you can consider it and let it sink in. So you can smell the words and their meanings like perfume... Everything was just so poetic. <br/><br/>Author <u>Hannah Harrington is only 23</u> and honestly, I am beyond impressed. To be that young and yet manage to write such a book? The girl is amazing. <br/><br/>Now, the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText10126268029077977690" style="display:none">Original review 2012:<br /><br /><i>" He took his pain and turned it into something beautiful " </i><br /><br />Harrington's writing is the kind that makes you stop while you're reading - just to re-read a sentence, to say it out loud, so you can consider it and let it sink in. So you can smell the words and their meanings like perfume... Everything was just so poetic. <br /><br />Author <u>Hannah Harrington is only 23</u> and honestly, I am beyond impressed. To be that young and yet manage to write such a book? The girl is amazing. <br /><br />Now, the book in itself.<br /><br /><b>I really, really liked Laney</b>. I know, right? It's weird that I focus like this on her but I can't help it. It's like she's all I can think about when I think about the book. But I loved <i>everything</i> about her. She was so sweet and funny and heart-breaking and just... I don't know. True. <br />I liked Harper, too. Kind of. And Jake. They feel right together.<br /><br />Actually the only flaw of this book is the fact that it reminded me too much of two others YA books. <br /><br />* The first one is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8470445.Fall_for_Anything" title="Fall for Anything by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Fall For Anything</a>, by Courtney Summers. Am I the <u>only one</u> out there who noticed how much those two books are alike ? <br /><br />They both feature a <b>teenage girl</b> who's had to deal with a close family member committing suicide <b>unexpectandly</b>. Both have to deal with the question "why?" and their mothers being close to a catatonic state, AND with the arrival at home of an aunt/friend that the main character can't stand. <br />Both heroines go on a <b>road trip</b> in order to understand, and ultimately overcome grief, <b>with some mysterious guy they're never seen before</b> but who seems to have known the dead person. Said guy <b>becomes the love interest</b>. At the end, he reveals a <b>huge secret</b> about the dead person. <br />AND, in both books, <b>photography</b> is a main topic. <br />No really, it's confusing when you come to think about it. <br /><br />It also made me think about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1314332.Before_I_Die" title="Before I Die by Jenny Downham" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Die</a>, by Jenny Downham, because of the relationship between Harper and Laney that was so similar Tessa and Zoey's : the narrator describes herself as plain, and her best friend as blond, hot, and kinda slutty. The BF is funny, always here to make some jokes or organize some crazy plans, yet she remains lovable and cute. AND, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the BF gets pregnant - consequence of her sleeping around. Which by the way, left me thoughtful. Was it really important for Laney to get pregnant? When, at the end, she just loses the baby so it's like it never happened? It felt like the easy way out, like she doesn't really have to take a decision, or really to do anything about it. Somehow it felt a bit useless. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I liked June, too. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The letter she left made me cry, the "PS- I'm not scared anymore" broke my heart. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I liked her a lot.<br /><br />And, other reviewers pointed that out too, but I think it was sort of selfish and unrealistic for Harper to steal June's ashes from her parents. I mean, okay for the road trip, sure, but she should have called them once she was in California to let them know about her project. They could have joined her to spill the ashes together. They knew June had always wanted to go to California. It's weird that Harper did it all herself.. like her parents didn't have the right to be there? <br /><br />Okay, now that said, it remains <b>a fantastic book</b>. Also I spent like 2 hours collecting all the musics of the playlists, and that's an aspect of the book I absolutely adored. <br /><br />4 stars.<br /><br /><br />Edit 2015: <br /><br />So I re-read it and didn't like it as much as I thought as I would. It just seemed very juvenile, not really like what I thought I remembered it to be. And I hated all these political messages that were forced down the reader's throat : environment, same sex relationships, religion, even about the music : the rant about whether punk is dead or the value of radio-music. Please. That wasn't any of the characters, that was all Hannah Harrington, and it wasn't subtle at all, it felt heavy and unnecessary. And the book didn't focus on June as much as it focused on HARPER&amp;JAKE - them snapping at each other even though you totally see the romance coming, and stupid unbelievable plots to have them sleep in the same bed or spend time together (like Laney being conveniently asleep or wandering around for half of the book so that they're oh-so-surprisingly left alone. Meh. I guess 3 years ago I had loved the romance, and now maybe I was looking for something deeper. And Harper was way too angsty and annoying (hoodies and black/red nail polish? Really?) <br /><br />And then there has got to be a problem when you agree with Aunt Helen, aka the character you're supposed to hate? I didn't agree with the religious aspect of her rants (and I thought that Harper was so unnecessarily disdainful when it came to that), but I do think that Harper was incredibly selfish and that it wasn't up to her to decide what to do with June's ashes. The whole road trip felt unrealistic. I don't know. I felt the "Young" in "Young Adult" very strongly this time. <br />2.5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10126268029077977690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_696292238" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696292238" />
    <a title="lily ☁️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10148904-lily"><img alt="lily ☁️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517405104p2/10148904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696292238?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lily ☁️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lily ☁️" href="/user/show/10148904-lily">lily ☁️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=best-romance">best-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=tolino">tolino</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=best-bfs">best-bfs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=heartache">heartache</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=beautiful-prose">beautiful-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=impressions">impressions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=sensitive-issues">sensitive-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10148904-lily?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696292238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12779415316075523603">Before you read my review, which consists of gushing, and gushing alone (you’ve been warned), let me tell you one thing: I’m not easily impressed by books. I so rarely give a book five stars, even one I love, that you could say I <i>never</i> do, and as of now, my average rating here on Goodreads is 2.63. But <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10947600.Saving_June' title='Saving June by Hannah Harrington' rel='nofollow noopener'>Saving June</a>—it blew me away.<br/><br/>I had a whole review written down—about the fantastic build-up, the characters, the relationships— everything. But when I finished, and was ready to post it, I realized</span>
  <span id="freeText12779415316075523603" style="display:none">Before you read my review, which consists of gushing, and gushing alone (you’ve been warned), let me tell you one thing: I’m not easily impressed by books. I so rarely give a book five stars, even one I love, that you could say I <i>never</i> do, and as of now, my average rating here on Goodreads is 2.63. But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10947600.Saving_June" title="Saving June by Hannah Harrington" rel="nofollow noopener">Saving June</a>—it blew me away.<br /><br />I had a whole review written down—about the fantastic build-up, the characters, the relationships— everything. But when I finished, and was ready to post it, I realized that none of my words of praise could ever even come close to representing the brilliance of this book. I don’t have the words in me to illustrate just exactly how unique and utterly impressive the journey of reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10947600.Saving_June" title="Saving June by Hannah Harrington" rel="nofollow noopener">Saving June</a> was, much as the main character, Harper Scott. She’s not your usual teenage girl by far; she’s sassy and she’s bold, she doesn’t care about trying to fit in, much the opposite, actually, and she has morals and principles she sticks to. Harper captured my heart from the first page, and so did her best friend, Laney. Unlike so many other superficial high school friendships you encounter in young-adult literature, their friendship was genuine and special, and they had each other’s backs. No backstabbing, no jealousy, no melodrama.<br /><br />And Jake—you couldn’t <i>not</i> fall in love with him, or with Jake and Harper. Their relationship wasn’t that mushy, corny, and very much overdone romance I’ve gotten so used to finding in young-adult novels. It was real, it was messy, and it was complicated, but it was the kind of complicated that was based on real issues, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4086928.Hannah_Harrington" title="Hannah Harrington" rel="nofollow noopener">Hannah Harrington</a> did such a wonderful job of building up their relationship.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10947600.Saving_June" title="Saving June by Hannah Harrington" rel="nofollow noopener">Saving June</a> was stunningly beautiful. It invoked so many different emotions in me; incredible sadness and grief, joy, love, melancholy, hope, and happiness. It’s definitely a book that makes you think about life, and draws you to a deeper appreciation for the things you have, but the message is subtly integrated in between the pages, as opposed to being forced down your throat, which I immensely appreciated. I’m not someone who cries when reading a book, but this book brought tears to my eyes, more than once.<br /><br />I'm not sure if I’ll ever find a novel that will move me as much, or at least not in the same way, as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10947600.Saving_June" title="Saving June by Hannah Harrington" rel="nofollow noopener">Saving June</a> did ever again, but I certainly hope so. My future novels certainly have a lot to live up to.<br /><br /><a href="https://sprinklesofdreams.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/sprinkles-dreams-19449885" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sprinklesofdreamsx/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://sprinklesofdreams.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/sprnklsofdreams" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>

<div id="review_344620406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344620406" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344620406?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848450950" href="/book/show/13640210-saving-june">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344620406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5315423822203093808">Even though this book is ultimately about loss and dealing with grief, it's a very diverting read filled with life, humor, and romance. Being a road trip story, be prepared for some amusing sightseeing along with plenty of colorful characters.<br/><br/>Saving June begins very powerfully during the aftermath of June's death. Harper finds herself in a bubble of grief, unable to even begin to understand why her sister killed herself. I could feel her heartache, as if it was my own. The emotional turmoil is e</span>
  <span id="freeText5315423822203093808" style="display:none">Even though this book is ultimately about loss and dealing with grief, it's a very diverting read filled with life, humor, and romance. Being a road trip story, be prepared for some amusing sightseeing along with plenty of colorful characters.<br><br>Saving June begins very powerfully during the aftermath of June's death. Harper finds herself in a bubble of grief, unable to even begin to understand why her sister killed herself. I could feel her heartache, as if it was my own. The emotional turmoil is extremely vivid and I was sure we were in for an overwhelmingly sad novel, but once the road trip begins it turns into a pleasant, beautiful story. After the initial explosion, though, the pacing can leave a bit to be desired until about half way. However, this leaves room for excellent character development and an incredibly sweet budding romance. <br><br>Extremely character oriented, Saving June brings forth a lot of vibrant personalities. Harper, herself, is frustrated and broken by her sister's death, making her a very gripping, sympathetic protagonist. The two main supporting roles, Jake and Laney, both have distinct personalities that are very different from each other. We see them go from snappy to charismatic. Thus, there was bound to be some banter and disagreements, but they have this wonderful chemistry that makes them seem naturally connected to each other. We then have a band of eccentric characters that we meet along the way that range from charming to outlandish. <br><br>So powerful that it's a character in itself, the music reverberates through the pages making it an important entity. It plays an immense part in Harper's healing process. This book is filled with musical references that will capture any music buff. Although I was familiar with a lot of the music mentioned, it's not to such a degree that made the frequent exchanges and debates mean as much as I think it should have. Nevertheless, its strong influence is undeniable. <br><br>As in the beginning, the conclusion yields a lot of emotional outbursts; it's an intense, piercing ending. Some parts of it do feel a bit too convenient, but I was satisfied with it overall. Are you a music fanatic? Do you enjoy road trips? Brilliant characterization? Poignant story lines? Saving June will take you and enrapture you all through to the end!<br><br>--<br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358334i/709537.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5315423822203093808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_185489226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2327078-k"><img alt="K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357523905p2/2327078.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373210244" href="/book/show/9672990-saving-june">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=ok-i-cheated">ok-i-cheated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=21st-cent">21st-cent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=ok-fine-its-ya">ok-fine-its-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185489226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13761759864505945862">And thus, the reason why I sometimes really hate first narrative. I am of the minority: <i>Saving June</i> has failed to awe me into an emotional chokehold, which seems to be the general denouement to the reading experience of many readers out there. This book, to its unfortunate luck, contains many reading pet peeves of mine. Sadly, there were so many things that bugged me about the way it was presented that I couldn't concentrate on the story itself. Although, to be completely and utterly truthful, I</span>
  <span id="freeText13761759864505945862" style="display:none">And thus, the reason why I sometimes really hate first narrative. I am of the minority: <i>Saving June</i> has failed to awe me into an emotional chokehold, which seems to be the general denouement to the reading experience of many readers out there. This book, to its unfortunate luck, contains many reading pet peeves of mine. Sadly, there were so many things that bugged me about the way it was presented that I couldn't concentrate on the story itself. Although, to be completely and utterly truthful, I don't think it would've made much difference to how I am ultimately rating this now. (I say all this with much respect, much respect).<br /><br />First off, the first person narrative and why I hate it: you can't get out of the character's head. You're stuck, for better for worse, for richer for poorer, etc. You have no defense against the onslaught of perpetual reflection. Harper said and explained, analyzed and hypothesized every degree of emotion that passed through her angsty, rock-solid but essentially vulnerable-in-a-strong-way, sixteen year old body. Everything. From her parents' divorce, to her antagonizing aunt Helen, to how she was always in June's shadow, to how far she and June have drifted apart, to how she hates June for killing herself but still misses her and loves her, to Laney and their yin-yang but somehow opposites attract kind of friendship, to Jake and all <i>that</i> jazz...I have a problem when a character talks too much. I keep saying this, but I love dialogue. And action. I don't want to just sit there and be told what a character is feeling. I don't need to know (and an author doesn't have to tell) everything a character is going through. It's too much. By "too much", I don't mean too much to read but I mean too much information that it takes away the reader's involvement. <br /><br />And here is where I am contradicting myself. As obviously pointed out by reviews I've read, people <i>were</i> emotionally invested -- so what am I saying? I just mean, a reader is not merely a "reader". We don't just sit there and read and nod and believe. We participate. There are scenes we read (and visualize in our heads) and its like a searching game...we read and we recognize small gestures that hold so much truth about a person's inside, words that reveal rooted secrets despite their seemingly trivial and insignificant initial impact, and its those details that unveil our clouded minds and deliver to us epiphanies about the characters (I'm thinking Melina Marchetta...Jellicoe Road, specifically). We read between the lines, we cover the gray areas, we fill in the blanks. Its like catching someone doing something from the corner of your eye and you think, <i>ha, gotcha!</i> If we're told everything, all the work is done for us. I want to see their pain, not hear about it.<br /><br />But enough with that. I've spent enough lines on one narrative complaint. Also, I'm sure none of you understood a single word. <br /><br />Anyway, I have more to whine about. This is a case where the author is so pervasively in your face that I can't focus on the fiction anymore. Music to politics to first-time sex to feminism to organized religion to how parents are just as screwed up as their teenage kids. Oh, but not these youths...they hold intellectual debates over bonfires. I don't have a problem with that. Its nice to see young characters stand up for their beliefs, but its not the characters, though, is it? Its Hannah Harrington. She has so much to say about everything that she's given up a section of her brain, each targeting a different field, to each one of her characters. In this case, write an essay. Or just a rant and post it on a blog. You don't have to write an entire YA novel and get it published for the masses -- what a hassle.<br /><br />The music. The incessant barrage of name/song dropping was making me choke on air. The discussion on the spiritual death of punk, to the manufactured, over-processed, "fast food for the ears" products of major pop labels...yappi yappi yap. We get it, its hip to listen to old school and unenlightened to listen to Top 40. Just like how its original to be vintage and generic to shop at Forever 21. (Let me make it clear, I listen and adore much of the music mentioned in said book and I shop both at thrift stores and XXI). This is an obvious social commentary on the state of youth today, except that we've heard it all before and its exhausting.<br /><br />I found everything Harrington was saying too judgmental, hasty and demeaning. How, for example, Aunt Helen turns to God because she has nothing else in her life. Harsh, much? If that's all she has to cling on to, then so be it. Don't turn them into caricatures. And I felt she did that with many of the characters: Aunt Helen, her parents, Laney...<br /><br />This is all without even addressing that fact that Harper stole her sister's urn! Come on, child! Think! Her justification for her "road trip" was far too fickle for me to even consider buying. That was not for Harper to decide.<br /><br />But here's the thing, sometimes Harrington says something blindingly pretentious, then does something to make me believe that she <i>knows</i> she's being pretentious and that, perhaps, this is actually a satire, or some higher work of fiction, not simply a teen book. But then she goes back to being pretentious and then I heave a sigh and roll me eyes...<br /><br />I'm going to end it here. I don't want this to sound anymore of a "hatey" review than it already does. If anyone is left feeling offended, that was not my intent. I just had to...but maybe that's how Harrington felt, and since this review can be seen as a judgement on her, then I'm a hypocrite. So, really, who the fuck am I to say anything at all?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13761759864505945862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer329674801" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8245297090806733768">OMG! Instant music geek orgasm! <br/><br/>Go request this on netgalley. Or read it. Now, now, now!<br/><br/>How awesome is this book? It made me forget exam anxiety. It made me forget my surroundings. It made me sit my arse down and read, from start to finish, and all I can say is, thank goodness I didn't open the file BEFORE I went into exams because I would have surely missed it.<br/><br/>"Saving June" tells the story of Harper, a girl whose sister has just committed suicide. The two girls have been dealing with the fallou</span>
  <span id="freeText8245297090806733768" style="display:none">OMG! Instant music geek orgasm! <br><br>Go request this on netgalley. Or read it. Now, now, now!<br><br>How awesome is this book? It made me forget exam anxiety. It made me forget my surroundings. It made me sit my arse down and read, from start to finish, and all I can say is, thank goodness I didn't open the file BEFORE I went into exams because I would have surely missed it.<br><br>"Saving June" tells the story of Harper, a girl whose sister has just committed suicide. The two girls have been dealing with the fallout of their parents' divorce for a long time, and June's death, coupled with their absentee father, really throws Harper off-balance. As an extra slap to the face, June was one of those perfect girls who everyone wants to emulate, and Harper, troublemaker extraordinaire, finds it impossible to fill her shoes. <br><br>When she learns that her parents will split her sister's ashes, Harper employs the help of her friend Laney to steal the urn and scatter them over the Pacific Ocean. The only problem? They have no car. Enter Jake, a friend of June whom she has never talked of previously, who seems to know more than he lets on about her suicide. The three embark on a cross-country trip that not only helps Harper discover some important things, but also for her to come to terms with her sister's decision and the reprecussions of it. <br><br>This is one of those books whose pros more than outshine its flaws. It isn't perfect, but then again, neither is life. I loved Harper's voice - it was brutally honest, yet sincere, and it does a fantastic job at conveying her character. She's lost, but doesn't lose direction, and is much more insightful than her parents, or her very religious aunt, give her credit for.<br><br>The banter was also fantastic, fresh and full of music references that made my little heart beat with glee. I had to physically restrain myself from compulsively quoting this thing on GR, because I thought my friend list would not appreciate the sudden influx of status updates on their dash. Suffice to say, it rocks.<br><br>Also, Jake is an ABBA fan. What's ABBA, you may ask? Well, only the soundtrack to my childhood! Having them referenced in this book, by a guy... <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380377761ra/733137.gif" width="500" height="233" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> I love ABBA. I also happen to love Jenna Marbles. The two things aren't connected, but that gif fucking rocks. </i><br><br>I'm not kidding when I say that this book is a multi-medium experience, even if it doesn't come with a set of built-in speakers... though it should... The music references, classic rock specifically, rival only <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7818683.Five_Flavors_of_Dumb" title="Five Flavors of Dumb by Antony John" rel="nofollow noopener">Five Flavors of Dumb</a> on the epic scale. It's a dream, especially when, like myself, you've grown up listening to those classic bands. Also? The version I got came with a playlist at the end. I predict that I won't be the only one playing "Let It Be" on a loop after finishing this.<br><br>There are some problematic bits, of course. There always are. But I was willing to overlook them, simply because the overall story blew me away.<br><br>What? Why are you still standing there? Go read this book! Naow!<br><br>Note: A copy was provided by the publishers via NetGalley. I strongly predict I will producre my own copy as soon as this becomes available.</span>

<div id="review_162520784" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2245895-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341463199p2/2245895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162520784?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/2245895-emily">Emily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2245895-emily?shelf=swoon">swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2245895-emily?shelf=characters-i-love">characters-i-love</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162520784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6463074077370255405">Hannah Harrington's amazing debut is a must-read for YA lovers. I haven't read a teen novel this fresh and wonderful in such a long time. It was a great book to read over my break. <br/><br/>Here's a quote from early in the book, that I think captures the tone of the novel perfectly and shows you Harper's personality. <br/><br/><i>"Jay, you should play something," Gwen suggests from across the crackling fire. Somehow from the way she says it, and the dark look Jake gives her in response, I can tell a gauntlet has been</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6463074077370255405" style="display:none">Hannah Harrington's amazing debut is a must-read for YA lovers. I haven't read a teen novel this fresh and wonderful in such a long time. It was a great book to read over my break. <br /><br />Here's a quote from early in the book, that I think captures the tone of the novel perfectly and shows you Harper's personality. <br /><br /><i>"Jay, you should play something," Gwen suggests from across the crackling fire. Somehow from the way she says it, and the dark look Jake gives her in response, I can tell a gauntlet has been thrown. Maybe some</i> You Got Served <i>style dance-off shenanigans will ensue. That would be - well, that would be pretty awesome, actually.</i><br /><br />The romance in this book made me grin while I was reading. I won't give away any spoilers, but page 219 (of the first Australian paperback edition) was my fave romantic part. *girly sigh*<br /><br />The book is non-stop action up until the last few chapters. It then slows down and you wonder why it is taking so long to finish. When I got to the end I knew why: It was Harper's story. If the book had ended earlier it really would've been June's story. <br /><br />The music references are used perfectly in this book, moving the plot and character development along quite nicely. I loved hearing a shout out to Harper's To Kill A Mockingbird namesake, and was excited to see the name of my musical hero Jeff Buckley. <br /><br />If you do read Saving June, please let me know what you think! <br /></span>

<div id="review_702614982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/702614982" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/702614982?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=roadtrip">roadtrip</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=sounds-like-a-movie">sounds-like-a-movie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=suicide">suicide</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer702614982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9429633833833855797"><i>
  <b>3 STARS</b>
</i><br/><br/><a href='http://www.flickr.com/photos/67647245@N07/9611583559/' title='3vmeqn by tina Ceballos, on Flickr' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434180i/874225.jpg' width='360' height='239' alt='3vmeqn' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>What do you do?<br/><br/><b>WHAT DO YOU DO?!?!</b><br/><br/>Well duh, kidnap her urn and take a roadtrip to California with your best friend and some random "douche-baggy hipster music snob with the taste of a forty-year old white guy" of course. The latter, by the way, also needs to fulfill the minimum requirement of being "sorta hot", owning a van named after a singer who OD-ed in heroin (because he's cool like that), mad skills in the dance floor and a shroud of mystery in his connection to suicidal sis.</span>
  <span id="freeText9429633833833855797" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>3 STARS</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/67647245@N07/9611583559/" title="3vmeqn by tina Ceballos, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434180i/874225.jpg" width="360" height="239" alt="3vmeqn" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What do you do?<br><br><b>WHAT DO YOU DO?!?!</b><br><br>Well duh, kidnap her urn and take a roadtrip to California with your best friend and some random "douche-baggy hipster music snob with the taste of a forty-year old white guy" of course. The latter, by the way, also needs to fulfill the minimum requirement of being "sorta hot", owning a van named after a singer who OD-ed in heroin (because he's cool like that), mad skills in the dance floor and a shroud of mystery in his connection to suicidal sis.<br><br>This should have been an easy sell to me. I love road trip stories. Old people music is heavily integrated in the plot (The Beatles!) and the snappy, witty banter between her characters, I'm starting to recognize as a Hannah Harrington trademark, was beyond amusing. Plus there's a somber, melancholic promise of delivering the feels with Harper being the troublesome, darker sister trying to figure out why her near-perfect sister just one day decided to kill herself. <br><br>But something in the way she moves (see what I did there?)… makes me want to shake Harper into the future. So we could skip the teenage angst, the road trip lessons from the mosh pit (in a punk concert. Seriously.), the protest rally and Fridgehenge to get to the part where she becomes the remarkable woman I already know she will become.<br><br>Have you ever thought about those books that we've read with the awesome, battle-scarred heroines who spout chockfull of wisdom and worldly views? You ever wonder how they got there? <br><br>This felt like the chronicles of that painful birthing process. Because at one point, those strong women we all agree to be a benchmark of cool and amazingness went through sixteen. And the thought process of angry, sixteen year old Harper is rife with self-esteem issues, egocentric notions and hormonally driven decisions that challenges my patience and understanding. But add in the grief and my limit has been exceed.<br><br>Because there were just one too many "woe is me" moments where Harper competes with the memory of June, followed by missing her sister, followed by being angry at herself for being helpless and rounding up nicely to placing some misplaced blame on everyone around her for not understanding her.<br><br>It's easily excused as her coping mechanism, yes but that doesn't mean I have to like it.<br><br>There's also an inexplicable amount of cheese and cliche that shouldn't be cheesy and cliched to anyone else but me, I guess. Because its probably just the Beatle fan snob in me that cringed when they sang along to <i>Hey Jude</i> in the van (it's a great song but you have an audiophile in the van and we couldn't have chosen something less… kitschy for the scene?) or when Harper broke down while listening to <i>Let It Be</i>.<br><br>There was also some stereotyping that didn't feel well with me. <u>
  <b>The divorcee aunt who Harper alleges to turn to religion as a crutch</b>
</u> was painted to be disfavored. The <u>
  <b>dreadlocked, pot-smoking friend </b>
</u> will sell a Hendrix memorabilia because its not Bob Marley. Jake's <u>
  <b>Bitchy Ex-girlfriend who trades the activist lifestyle for college</b>
</u>?<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"She created this papier-mâché Jesus - except it's Jesus as a woman - and there are high heels instead of nails through the hands. And there's a tampon stuffed in Jesus' mouth."</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Which of course represents "women's oppression due to traditionally gendered beauty standards driven by patriarchy".<br><br>But I can never deny Hannah Harrington's gift for dialogue. Easily among the sharpest and wittiest I've read so far in the genre. Which makes an excellent tool to draw her protagonists closer, thankfully <u>
  <b>avoiding the hateful insta-love pitfall</b>
</u>. There's a scattered quality to the message it was trying to to drive but the clever banter between her characters shines through, even when it's Harper and Jake bickering and bent on making the road trip end up in hell or a ditch somewhere.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"I can't believe you saw me puke," I groan pulling the blankets over my head.<br>"It was a lovely moment," he says drily. "Now there's a band name for you - the Lovely Pukes."<br>I poke my head back out to shoot him a withering look. "How about the Shut the Fuck Ups?"<br>"The Toilet Huggers."<br>"The Imminent Castrations."<br>"Yes, with out debut album - Lorena Bobbitt, How Could You."</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>So I'm pretty happy I read <i>Speechless</i> ahead of this one because I'm not sure I'd have picked that up if I started with this but the reasons are more of my own personal quirks. I can see this being favorite-shelved by someone and not feel judgy towards the reader because I can totally see twenty-something me being all over this. I never thought I'd see the day when I'd feel too old for a YA/NA book but this may just did it. <br><br>One last thing, I don't see how Jake's ABBA love as the quirk this book made it to be… in my side of the universe that's not quirky. <br><br>That's just going with nature. #fuckyeahABBA</span>
  <a data-text-id="9429633833833855797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8C/X+XaHn5xXpSkMtMYhNqdWdsjm8l4/PSk8h6CpcAvunSN/uFm60CxXV4y4Y+3ndwmnw21r54JnXZTF6OU4oQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zwXQ77LEd4msNaH5l70630YRtcrlGejcVsAIiWbzbF/RtyRpfBpSxdfH33mbGPYOlk5kwW6AUWEMtKDLLr8k9Q==')})
  }
//]]>
